    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2630734351" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2630734351" />
    <a title="Aqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44266986-aqua"><img alt="Aqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502852541p2/44266986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2630734351?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aqua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aqua" href="/user/show/44266986-aqua">Aqua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781534427334" href="/book/show/43822791-legacy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44266986-aqua?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44266986-aqua?shelf=guilty-pleasure-books">guilty-pleasure-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2630734351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18215558073820095346"><b>So 8 books in to a 9(?) book series and it feels less like there's been any actual plot progression and more like I'm sitting through my local theater's annual 24hr marathon of the movie <i>Groundhog Day</i>.</b> <i>Legacy</i> is undeniably better than <i>Flashback</i> (low bar), if only because of the shift of focus to Keefe over Fitz, but I'm still so frustrated with this series. This doesn't <i>feel</i> like a late-in-the-series book. We just go through the same paces we've gone through in the last 7 books in which Sophie a</span>
  <span id="freeText18215558073820095346" style="display:none"><b>So 8 books in to a 9(?) book series and it feels less like there's been any actual plot progression and more like I'm sitting through my local theater's annual 24hr marathon of the movie <i>Groundhog Day</i>.</b> <i>Legacy</i> is undeniably better than <i>Flashback</i> (low bar), if only because of the shift of focus to Keefe over Fitz, but I'm still so frustrated with this series. This doesn't <i>feel</i> like a late-in-the-series book. We just go through the same paces we've gone through in the last 7 books in which Sophie and her gang attempt to investigate things and 800 pages of filler later are outsmarted at every turn and the overall plot goes nowhere. <br /><br />I was far more forgiving of this lack of plot progression back in book 3 or 4, but we are on book 8 now!!! Sigh... let's be positive for a minute. We have an interesting conflict set up here. In the very beginning we are finally, <i>finally</i>, given a general overview of the Neverseen's overarching plan. I like what the author is <i>trying</i> to say, that holing up in isolation based on nationality is not a long-term solution to anything. Every scene Keefe is in is still awesome as usual. I won't deny my boy Keefe is really the shining star keeping me in this series, and I need to see him get his due. I still like the side characters when they are actually given anything to do (oh, poor Linh) and Stina also becomes a member of the Sophie gang in this book as well, which I enjoyed. The author also deftly reminds you of relevant plot points throughout the novel as they come up in case you've forgotten over the last 4714 (yep, I counted) pages in this incredibly convoluted plot, and it's much appreciated. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought Sophie's scenes with Oralie after the whole mother reveal were very well done as well. It's an understandably complex relationship shown in a complex way. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall though... it's just same old, same old. It feels like I'm reading the same book and writing the same review over and over again. There's enough entertainment and Keefe to keep me going, but the same things that annoy me continue to annoy me. There is still a lot of potential in this series, but it doesn't feel like the author's writing is growing and it's <i>frustrating</i>. I really <i>want</i> to like this series more. I just wish it would pick up the pace.<br /><br />Ok, so now... well there's a lot to unpack here.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First of all, <b>THEY GET OUTSMARTED BY THE NEVERSEEN AT EVERY TURN AGAIN ARE YOU FUCKING KIDDING ME?!</b><br /><br />*DEEP BREATHS*<br /><br /><b>Why do the heroes suck?</b><br />One of the major issues is even 8 books in we're still following the formula of our heroes investigate some stuff, find out very little, and then just react to whatever the Neverseen throw at them while being outsmarted. Despite all the allies Sophie has accumulated, they only succeed at saving Keefe in the end because of Deus Ex Glimmer. All they do is react to the Neverseen and we spend most of the books <i>not</i> taking any action against them. At one point I had hope for Linh's plan to find them, but then they just dropped it. It's <i>frustrating</i>.<br /><br /><b>Self-aware?</b><br />The author frequently throws in this meta-commentary about how little our heroes have accomplished and how often they lose, so it <i>seems</i> like she is self-aware, but then it all leads nowhere. By the climax all they've managed to learn in 700ish pages is that Gisela took some kind of treatment and that the dwarven magsidian is involved in the Neverseen's plot somehow. And then they just get their asses handed to them yet again. Sophie doesn't even use a single ability during the "climactic fight," if you can even call it that. <br /><br />We also, hilariously, get meta-commentary on how much talking these characters do. Which is just really ironic considering this conversation takes place over 700 pages of filler in. <blockquote><i>Sophie hadn't been paying attention, since it was basically the same conversation they'd had before the Celestial Festival - in that exact same room, no less - with everyone fighting over who should and shouldn't go, and trying to anticipate what the Neverseen were planning. <br /><br />They'd had an equally long debate before their venture into Nightfall - <i>and</i> before the ogre Peace Summit in Lumenaria. <i>And</i> before they'd headed into Ravagog. <i>And</i> before they'd tried to ambush the Neverseen on Mount Everest. <br /><br />Even the night Sophie had gone to have her abilities healed had taken all kinds of discussion. That's what they did. Overanalyze. Overprepare. And it never worked. <i>We can't keep doing this</i>.</i></blockquote>We really need an editor in here to pick up the pace. It would be one thing if that page time was spent on developing the side characters, but instead every scene is just riddled with so much filler. The vast majority of the first 30% of this book is spent on this stupid regency stuff along with endless discussions about clothes and cloaks and pins and crowns and makeup and team names. There is no reason we had to spend over 200 pages on this. This book has no excuse to be this long.<br /><br /><b>How many more times must I be subjected to scenes like these:</b><br />1) Fitz walking in on Sophie and Keefe in a compromising(?) situation.<br />2) Conversations about whether or not Sophie should be allowed to go somewhere (she always does end up going wherever is under discussion so these are pointless)<br />3) Conversations about which bodyguards should accompany Sophie. (Who fucking cares)<br />4) Conversations where characters get mad about being left out of something. (This is like twice a chapter for goodness sake)<br />5) Conversations where Sophie hypocritically tries to convince one of her friends that they shouldn't take a risk, even though they will of course proceed to do exactly that without fail.<br />6) Conversations where Sophie feels like a freak or a failure and the 5 million people who love her reassure her how loved and special she is. <br />7) Sophie finding out about another hidden or malfunctioning ability or getting a new gadget or piece of jewelry to control one of her many abilities.<br />8) Sophie having to convalesce for ages after an injury/ability reset.<br />9) Characters teasing Sophie about the love triangle or commenting on her obliviousness.<br />10) Good guy joins the Neverseen against his will and the good guys doubt his loyalty (can't believe this happened twice!)<br /><br /><b>Why are we still introducing new world-building?</b><br />It's one thing to explore a new city, but a lot of pretty crucial world-building elements are introduced here, and it is far too late for that. It's weird none of these things came up before and it leads to further plot convolution and dropped plot threads. Shadow flux was introduced in the previous book and in this book we get ethertine (which is actually introduced <i>DURING</i> the climax, don't even get me started on how clumsy that was). We even have a new villain introduced in the climax, because <i>that's</i> exactly what we needed at this point. *eyeroll* <br /><br />So shadow flux and ethertine are important, fine. But we're also introduced to a whole host of other things that just drop off a cliff (not even including all the plot threads from previous books that have been dropped).<br />1) The King's Path: Sophie just sidesteps it in the final escape.<br />2) Sophie's new inflicting powers: She uses them once and they accomplish nothing. Why does Sophie need to get a new/upgraded ability in every book? <br />3) All the Team Valiant stuff: It changed <i>nothing</i> for the overall plot and we spent <i>hundreds</i> of pages on it. The relevant characters didn't even get any development out of it.<br />4) The primary sources info dump.<br />5) All the London stuff: Literally nothing added to the plot except a pointless confrontation with Gisela.<br /><br /><b>I hate Fitz</b><br />I must say I really hate the trope of the main character being oblivious to everyone being in love with them. How could Sophie <i>not</i> figure out Keefe likes her? This is past normal humility and just plain stupidity. And don't even get me started on this conversation with Keefe: "You really think Fitz would be bothered by us working together?" Oh come <i>on</i> Sophie. Did you also somehow miss all of Fitz's jealous rages in the previous book? She even attempts to defend (excuse me while I vomit) Fitz's attempted (and apparently successful on a slower scale!) murder of Alvar. Not that he faces any consequences. But wait...<blockquote><i>Keefe did seem to have a way of helping Fitz keep control of his temper.</i></blockquote> OH ARE WE ACKNOWLEDGING IT NOW?! ... Except no, of course we're not. Fitz's obvious anger issues are still glossed over by everyone except the villains for some reason. Fitz also at one point makes Keefe paint a picture of Fitz and Sophie professing their love. I love how we're continually reminded that Fitz and Keefe are best friends when Fitz obviously doesn't care or give a shit about getting to know him.<br /><br /><b>The damn love triangle</b><br />The best part of this book was how little Fitz there was in it. And of course, my absolute favorite scene definitely has to be when they break up after Fitz refuses to accept Sophie as unmatchable. Real upstanding guy. But of course, instead of Sophie reflecting on how she deserves better in a partner, she makes up with Fitz at the end just because they "miss" each other. They agree to stay friends instead of dating, but of course the author <i>still</i> just can't let this damn love triangle go and has to throw a "for now" out there for all the Fitzphie fans. Ugh. At least it seems pretty obvious we're past the Fitzphie nonsense and on trajectory to Sophie realizing Keefe has been the partner she needed all along (although Keefe really deserves better).<br /><br /><b>Who needs principles when you have cute boys?</b><br />So I am still pissed about Sophie dropping her principles and signing up for the match in <i>Flashback</i>.<blockquote><i>"Am I supposed to be a poster-girl for the dark side of matchmaking?"<br />"Of course not. Though as I recall, you have had quite a few issues with the system. You even considered not participating"<br />She had. Matchmaking was disappointingly unromantic and inherently problematic. But that was before... She couldn't think about it without wanting to throw up. And yet her mind still flashed to a pair of beautiful teal eyes.</i></blockquote>Oh gag me. Hey girls, cute boys are worth giving up your principles for! Except, no, wait that's a horrible message to send! <br /><br />It does at least lead to the Fitzphie break up, which made me very happy. But unfortunately Sophie doesn't decide to stay unmatchable because she doesn't want to participate in a broken, judgmental system, but rather because of the chaos Oralie's reveal would cause... So we still never get a conversation about how unfair it was of Fitz to pressure her into it and how horrible the system is.<br /><br /><b>Bullying</b><br />So most stories trying to send a good message that include bullies would at some point have the main characters have a conversation about how they shouldn't stoop to the bully's level and should rise above and be kind, right? Not here.<blockquote><i>"Right, and you guys weren't already looking at me like you'd rather work with a muskog," Stina countered. <br />Dex flashed his most wicked grin. "A muskog <i>would</i> smell better." Grady coughed through another laugh - and Sandor's shoulders shook like he was holding in a fit of goblin giggles.</i></blockquote>So we're promoting bullying now? How else am I supposed to read this? Why are the adults laughing at such a stupid, juvenile joke? The books have set Stina up as a bully since the beginning, but it's highly concerning how the author seems to justify all the horrible things Sophie and her friends say in return with things like the adults laughing at jokes or no one pointing out that maybe they could try being the bigger people and be nice to Stina. I just felt bad for her in every scene she was in as Dex kept hurling insults her way<blockquote><i>"Why would you pick these losers for something so important?"<br />"Uh, because these <i>losers</i> have taken on the Neverseen how many times now?" Dex snapped back.<br />"And <i>lost</i> how many times?" Stina countered. "Oh, that's right - all of them."</i></blockquote>Stina speaks the truth though. I actually like her character and would like to know more about her, but you know... <br /><br /><b>The poor neglected side characters</b><br />I would gladly give up the endless pages upon pages spent upon pointless things that unnecessarily inflate these books to 800+ page tomes for a scene where Linh gets some development or is shown dealing with her brother's absence (she gets <b>one scene</b> for the first 95% of this book and doesn't show up again until the climax), or a scene where Sophie and Biana actually act like the friends we are told they are (or maybe Biana could even be allowed to focus on herself and talk about her crush on Dex), or scenes where Biana deals with the trauma of being horrifically scarred, or Marella deals with being an illegal pyrokinetic, or Linh and Marella bond over their powerful elemental powers (happens off screen), or Wylie and Linh talk (happens off screen), or... anything!!! <br /><br />We never get to have any scenes where the side characters' development or worries are the focus because the book is so focused on detailing every tiny worry that Sophie has. So when Maruca and Stina join the already incredibly large cast... I just... WHY!? Why do we need more characters that will just be ignored? <br /><br /><b>Humans</b><br />Still not a fan of how everything is just the stupid humans fault in bringing the planet to war/extinction. I mean, in reality, sure, that is 100% true, but in this world the elves have done plenty of horrible shit. At one point Dex comments on how silly it is that the humans divide themselves up into nations when they could be so much stronger together. Oh those silly humans. Why can't they be more like the special, oligarchical elves who enslave gnomes, split up the magical world by species, and maintain a rigid class structure based on special talent manifestation, noble status, and match status!<br /><br /><b>So what have we accomplished?</b><br />So 800 pages later, 2nd to last book in the series, outsmarted at every turn, what have we actually accomplished towards bringing this series to a conclusion? Well Keefe may or may not have a new ability and... our heroes are no closer to stopping the Neverseen in any way, shape, or form. And yeah they've destabilized all the races, but it doesn't seem like the world is <i>that</i> unstable that a war would be brewing. The dwarves lost their king, but instantly replaced him. I'm just so confused where this series is going or how it intends to get there in only one more book (I guarantee it'll be extended). But, honestly, it really <i>needs</i> to start ramping things up here. The formula is getting old, and I'm so, so tired of the heroes being idiots. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="18215558073820095346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3093009057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76251049-lana"><img alt="Lana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579567868p2/76251049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3093009057?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana" href="/user/show/76251049-lana">Lana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7847224524536554180">I am just staring at the line "What did you think? Give a review!".<br/><br/>First off: I will not be reading any of the next books. <br/>That's how severely disappointing Shannon Messenger was.<br/>I am also disgusted by her writing and what style and theme her book has become<br/>Her first book was REALLY GOOD!!! Sure, Sophie was a little bit immature, but it was really good!<br/><br/>I should've seen this coming with Flashback; Shannon made little comments like "Oh, Sophie had <i>lots</i> of ideas of what she wanted to do with Fitz".</span>
  <span id="freeText7847224524536554180" style="display:none">I am just staring at the line "What did you think? Give a review!".<br /><br />First off: I will not be reading any of the next books. <br />That's how severely disappointing Shannon Messenger was.<br />I am also disgusted by her writing and what style and theme her book has become<br />Her first book was REALLY GOOD!!! Sure, Sophie was a little bit immature, but it was really good!<br /><br />I should've seen this coming with Flashback; Shannon made little comments like "Oh, Sophie had <i>lots</i> of ideas of what she wanted to do with Fitz". <br />Sure, she left this meaning unknown, but that's obviously a sexual meaning.<br />Now we come to this book, where Sophie OPENS THE DOOR TO A BOY'S ROOM WITHOUT HIM SAYING SHE CAN COME IN AND HE HAS HIS SHIRT OFF.<br />Excuse me? Is this a trashy, racy YA novel? Or is this for 8-12 year olds, like it says on the suggested inside flap.<br />Really Shannon? <i>Really?</i><br />I'm completely disgusted with this book. <br />What are you trying to teach younger kids? Even I don't want to read that stuff, and I'm a HUUUGE ROMANCE FREAK!!<br />Kasie West totally pulls romance off in a graceful way, but this? This was just gross.<br />If I may take a line from my good friend, I would "Burn this book for fuel and not even feel bad about it". <br />This has got to be the worst book I have read in ALL OF 2019.<br /><br />Here's a few more points:<br />Everything goes exactly right for Sophie<br />None of the characters have depth <br />All the characters have the same exact voice and talk the same and act the same and have the same sense of humor and are all sarcastic about everything and it gets <i>really</i> tiring.<br />She claims credit for J. R. R. Tolkien's writing.<br />She namedrops tons of stuff like Harry Potter and Howl's Moving Castle and Lord Of The Rings.<br />Her writing is immature and it felt like reading word vomit.<br /><br /><br />In short, these books could've been <i>great.</i><br />But Shannon, you've just lost a reader. And you're losing more, my friend used to buy your books right away, but she even stopped.<br />I cannot describe how revolted I am at this entire waste of paper, I don't think I've ever been this fired up about a book before.<br />Please Shannon, as my final plea, stop making trashy sexual themed novels and various hints for adults- in a CHILDREN'S BOOK.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7847224524536554180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2891150809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2891150809" />
    <a title="A." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99621363-a"><img alt="A." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575324650p2/99621363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2891150809?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="A." href="/user/show/99621363-a">A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781534427334" href="/book/show/43822791-legacy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=it-could-have-been-better">it-could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=too-much-talking-not-enough-plot">too-much-talking-not-enough-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=pleasantly-suprised">pleasantly-suprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=decent">decent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=mary-sue-mc">mary-sue-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=simplistic-writing">simplistic-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=a-bit-slow">a-bit-slow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99621363-a?shelf=obnoxious-heroine">obnoxious-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2891150809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14963085782150905289"><b>After eight books . . .<br/><br/>Over 4,500 pages . . .<br/><br/>And almost one million words into the series . . . <br/><br/>WE FINALLY KNOW, WHAT THE RESPECTIVE GOALS OF THE BLACK SWAN AND NEVERSEEN ARE.<br/><br/>YES!</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed this instalment. And I cannot believe that I am saying that after the disaster that was the previous book. I was expecting this book to be <b>extremely long winded, tedious, and boring.</b> Instead, <b>it was entertaining, engaging, and occasionally funny.</b><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Let’s get right into it and start at the beginning</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14963085782150905289" style="display:none"><b>After eight books . . .<br /><br />Over 4,500 pages . . .<br /><br />And almost one million words into the series . . . <br /><br />WE FINALLY KNOW, WHAT THE RESPECTIVE GOALS OF THE BLACK SWAN AND NEVERSEEN ARE.<br /><br />YES!</b><br /><br />I enjoyed this instalment. And I cannot believe that I am saying that after the disaster that was the previous book. I was expecting this book to be <b>extremely long winded, tedious, and boring.</b> Instead, <b>it was entertaining, engaging, and occasionally funny.</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Let’s get right into it and start at the beginning: <b>the start of this book is absolutely wonderful.</b> I think this book has the strongest beginning of all the books in the series. It started off just right; not in the middle of action, but at a time where you could easily follow what was going on and kept you engaged. However, around the hundred-page mark, I noticed that the <b>characterization of the characters was different.</b> Fitz was acting more like Dex, Dex was acting more like Keefe, and Sophie was acting more like Fitz.<br /><br /><b>The only character who sort of stayed the same was Keefe.</b> He was as wonderful as ever in this novel, but . . . I felt like <b>his reaction to his mother wanting to kill him was a bit calm.</b><br /><br />A bit . . . <i>too</i> calm.<br /><i><blockquote>Keefe watched her gloves fingers cover her palm, and for a second, he turned his hand and held on as tight as he could. Then he sighed and let go, scooting away from her. “I'm fine Foster. We all knew this was coming.”<br />“We did?” Ro asked, beating Sophie to the question.</blockquote></i> Ro and I had the same reaction.<br /><br />Say you just discovered that your mother wanted you dead. What would your first reaction to this be? I know for sure that it won't be similar to Keefe's.<br /><br />Initially, I thought it was shock, but he didn't linger on it too long and brought out these notebooks and started talking about his ideas to defeat the Neverseen. <b>I thought it was going to be addressed again later in the book, so I dropped it, but when the time came, it was <i>completely glossed over</i>.</b> Like, how did he feel about it? How was he dealing with it?? And most importantly, what was his father's reaction??? All of these things were barely touched upon. So, the whole thing kind of happened off ‘screen'. I want to believe that this is the author's way of showing the reader that Keefe is bottling up his emotions and is heading towards a mental breakdown, but I won’t hold my breath. I thought the same when Biana was badly injured by Vespera in <i>Nightfall</i>, and what came out of that? Nothing. So, I think the same will happen in Keefe’s situation. <b>It will only be brought up as the situation/plot requires it and Keefe will not grow from this in any way, shape, or form.</b> And we were barely shown how the other characters outside of Sophie reacted to this; it was all lost in The Quest to Find Sophie’s Biological Parents.<br /><br />Speaking of Biana, <b>she and Dex played a much larger role in instalment</b> – though I’m basing this off of Flashback, so the bar is not set very high. Messenger shed the spotlight on so many characters and she managed to do it in such a way that we didn’t get an overdose of any of them. Conversely though, Fitz, who is supposed to be a main character, had the reverse problem (not that I'm complaining). He was barely in any scenes and he wasn’t part of Team Valiant. <br /><br />Around this point, Team Valiant were introduced and they had their first mission. <b>And while I like the idea of Team Valiant, I just don’t understand why Sophie didn’t say no and give her role of leader to Fitz instead.</b> She has so many other things going on in her life; it would be next to impossible trying to juggle everything. The time that Sophie spent on missions for Team Valiant, would’ve been time that she used to training or researching things on the Neverseen. I loved the addition of Maruca and Stina to the main cast. <b>Maruca manifesting as Psionipath makes her very useful to the Black Swan</b>, though her introduction to Sophie's team feels awfully similar to another character in this series . . . While <b>I enjoyed that Stina was in the team</b>, I still don't understand why she was included; she's not in Sophie's main group. In spite of that, I truly enjoyed her insight and input. I think she is the most realistic and believable character in the series thus far. And while we're still on the subject on Team Valiant, Wylie’s father, <b>Prentice, Alden, Tiergan were strangely absent the entire novel.</b><br /><br />After Team Valiant comes back from the Paragon, they go their separate ways. Sophie meets with Keefe and the two begin talking about matchmaking . . . then <b>Fitz shows up just as Keefe mentioned that Sophie was unmatchable</b> . . . Mind you, Sophie hadn’t told Fitz anything about it. <br /><br /><b>And his reaction was much calmer than I thought it was going to be.<br /><br />Much, <i>much</i> calmer.</b><br /><br />I was expecting him to fly into rage-mode when he learned of it; which says everything you need to know about his character. Like smashing objects, screaming at Sophie, and hurling insults Keefe, but he took it in stride, and he sort of accepted it. <b>Don't get me wrong,</b> his reaction was terrible and he later began pressuring Sophie into getting the match, but overall, his reaction was considerably calmer than what I thought he was going to give. <br /><br /><b>I still don’t understand why Messenger is completely ignoring Fitz anger management issues.</b> The other characters seem aware of it, but they don’t do anything about it. Which is weird, because if this were Keefe, the other characters would be quick to shut it down. So why isn't Shannon doing the same for Fitz? In spite of that, think Sophie' taken off her rose-coloured glasses that she would wear when examining Fitz's behavior. She had many moments where she was annoyed with him, and actually fought back. A perfect example of this was when he was getting mad at her for not getting matched. I thought she was going to roll over and take it, but fortunately she didn't. Now all she needs to do is compare Fitz’s behavior to Keefe’s, have an epiphany, realize that Keefe is a much better fit for her, and start dating Keefe. <br /><br />And while were still on the subject of matchmaking, <b>I really hated the way Mr. Forkle handled the whole Sophie-being-unmatchable situation. He is literally denying Sophie the right to get married.</b> Now don’t get me wrong, I understand why Mr. Forkle is doing it, but it doesn't make the situation any less unfair. If he knew that telling Sophie her parents identities would change a lot of things, why didn't he make sure that her parents were the most unproblematic elves in existence? You would think a man as smart as Forkle would make sure of that, so he could avoid an issue like this. He knew what he was getting into when he chose to make a person. He knew that eventually she’d wanted to get married. In my opinion, <b>Sophie's reaction to the whole situation was completely understandable.</b> Though, I'll admit, she could've handled it much better. But she’s not some marionette that he has all the control over. The way he tried to spin the situation and make it seem like Sophie was the one in the wrong, was <b>infuriating</b>. He has taken away so many things from this girl – her safety, her mental health, her physical health – the least he could do is give her the names of her biological parents. The absolute least. <br /><br />Not long after this, Mr. Forkle comes to Havenfield to tell her the truth about her abilities. And I just have to say: <b>Sophie gaining two more abilities this instalment was incredibly plot device-y and unneeded</b>. The enhancing thing was just used to further the love triangle and the whole inflicting-beam-coming-out-of-her-forehead-thing looks stupid. I get that they are supposed to help her defeat the Neverseen and stuff, but even after she gained them abilities, she <b>barely used them in the final fight of this book</b>. What was the point of Sophie going through so much for two abilities that don't help her much outside of very specific situations? Is it to show the reader just how <i>pOwErFuL</i> and <i>speshullllll</i> and <i>dIfFeReNt</i> Sophie is? 'Cause we don't need to be reminded of that. I wouldn't be as annoyed if Shannon used the abilities to further the plot, but we both know they won't.<br /><br /><b>There was an abundance of world building this novel.</b> Seat of Eminence, the Paragon, and the Sources to name a few. I love world building as much as the next person, but just like Sophie’s new abilities, <b>it was unneeded</b>. The whole thing with Empath's-heart-stopping-three-times-when-they-lie is a perfect example of this. It was only used so Sophie could figure out that Oralie is her mother, and <b>I'm going to guess that it'll be used for Sophie to realize Keefe likes her and maybe be used in the search for her father.</b> But once it's served its purpose, it’ll become one of many plot points that Shannon will forget about and not do anything smart with. Going back to Oralie, I’m glad that Messenger went with the most logical option for who Sophie’s biological mother is.<b>Sophie's reaction to the whole thing was completely understandable. Sophie has every right to be mad at Oralie.</b> While I understand why Oralie didn't tell Sophie, she stood by and let some messed up things happen to Sophie to keep the secret a secret. <br /><br />Going back to the search for Sophie's biological parents, I don't understand why Biana did most of work. What Biana did was so sweet – don’t get me wrong - but it doesn’t make sense. Sophie’s been wondering who her parents are since the beginning of the series. When she’s presented an opportunity, she’s not just going to hand it over to Biana . . .<br /><br />Anyway, before I move on, I just want to say that <b>I think Tiergan is Sophie's biological father</b>.<br /><br />Around this time, the pace of the book really picked up. They realized that the magsidian crystals don’t react well to light (random detail that will be used once then dropped). Shortly after, Sophie and Co. discovered the person Keefe delivered the letter to: Ethan Benedict Wright II. I wouldn’t be surprised if Gisela was the one who murdered them (Wright and his daughter) but I don’t think they died at her hands specifically. What I mean is I don’t think she was who killed them directly, I just think she had someone else give the final blow. Either way, I really disliked how the whole thing was swept under the rug after a chapters worth of speculation. <br /><br />Sophie and Fitz then made the stupidest decision they have made in a long while: a sPoNtaNeoUS tRIp. More like a suicidal trip. Like you just learned that Gisela may also be capable of murder, in addition to her being a stealing, thieving, and conniving. And the first thing you do is go to London - without your bodyguards, if I might add - and try to go head to head with her?! <br /><br />The next two chapters after this were arguably <b>the most nuanced things</b> that Shannon has ever written. <br /><br />1. <b>Keefe’s father actually loving Keefe but not letting that love show because it complicates all the goals he had for him was just sad.</b> Keefe was deprived of a healthy, loving relationship with both his parents simply because they were obsessed with their goals for him. It’s one thing to have extremely high goals for yourself, but to force them on your child . . . It’s a miracle Keefe kept true to himself after all these years.<br /><br />2. <b>The whole Alvar-being-the-lesser-son-because-Fitz-is-the-only-Telepath situation was really sad too</b> (not that I feel bad for him, I just understood what he was saying). It was probably the most nuanced thing that Shannon has written this series. I want to believe that this is the opening of the floodgates of how-terrible-a-character-Fitz-actually-is, but I won’t hold my breath. Strangely though, when Alvar mentioned that Fitz is essentially the one responsible for his slow death, Sophie didn’t even comment on it. Didn’t even blink. <br /><br />Let’s move on to the “climax”. That was honestly <b>the most disappointing climax of this entire series</b>. It was literally just <b>talking</b>. Ten pages of Sophie talking to King Enki, him betraying them, and Keefe abilities being ‘reset’ (I’m not entirely sure what to call it). I thought Sophie and Co. were going to lose, but <b>Glimmer pulled a deus ex machina</b>; so technically, Sophie and Co. won, but not by their own wits. <b>Tam's plotline with the Neverseen was completely glossed over</b> (not surprised, knew that was going to happen). <b>We didn’t see any of the Neverseen besides Lady Gisela</b> (Sophie and Co. had split into two groups - Sophie's group went against Gisela and Fitz’s group went against everyone else). And apparently <b>Vespera wanted to lose . . .?</b> That part was glossed over too. Keefe’s abilities being 'reset' was cool and all, and I cannot wait to see what it turns out to be, but I just couldn’t bring myself to care about it. All I hope is that he is okay. <br /><br />Overall, the climax was disappointing and felt incredibly rushed. The only good thing I can say about it is that it finally got the balling rolling for Keefe's legacy. <br /><br /><b>I was just so happy when we learned what the goals of the Black Swan and Neverseen are.</b> <br /><br />The Black Swan: to save human beings and save the elven world from the Neverseen. <br /><br />The Neverseen: world domination.<br /><br />As ecstatic as I am about these new revelations, <b>this really should've happened in like book three or four.</b><br /><br />The book ended with <b>Sophie and Oralie getting ready to read one of the forgotten secrets.</b> All I hope is that the next book delves right into where this book left off, but I won’t be surprised if it didn’t. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I just don't know what to think of <i>Legacy</i> as a whole. It had it's issues, but it was definitely better than <i>Flashback.</i> <b>The beginning was wonderful and the pacing was nice</b> - even though it plateaued after the three-hundred-page mark. It was all bogged down by the endless discussions and useless world building things. I liked how <b>the writing felt different</b>; the characters don't sound like eleven-year-olds anymore. But <b>Mr. Forkle handling of the whole Sophie-being-unmatchable situation and Fitz’s ignored anger issues really angered me.</b> However, <b>the inclusion of so many more characters, the fact that five of the lingering plot questions were answered, and Keefe kind of made up for it.</b> <br /><br />In addition to that, I am scared for the next book. It's supposed to be the final book (there may be a tenth). But <b>this book didn't feel like it was the penultimate book in the series.</b> There are still a ton of unanswered questions and we're still nowhere when it comes to defeating the Neverseen.<br /><br />But taking everything into account . . . <b>I would rate <i>Legacy</i> 3.25 to 3.5 stars.</b><br /><br />(Written on Nov. 7th, 2019)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14963085782150905289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('672mLQQvRYvnsOiCLW5IwD3F16xTRwvfsQTEfmBFTGP5I5CFxn4n1CWUnzFZ3DtTvlfM7Vjz0jr7UhJHZoApRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1IrBvBbWc2kGekun0ZjpknJb7Ha2XJ3C5vNHAqBGu6DGFPcU1IcRNsRePBSlKpoB8cn3N73oRCespZE7poPehQ==')})
  }
//]]>

Necessari<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8048959794757518506\" style=\"display:none\">When Alex finds out he is Unwanted, he expects to die. That is the way of the people of Quill.
